Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** — the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 5. Feedback Collection\n\nAfter completion, collect implicit feedback:\n- Track if user overrode tier (implicit classification feedback)\n- Note smooth completion vs errors (quality signal)\n- Store for calibration learning\n\n## MCP Integration\n\n**Required Servers by Tier**:\n- STRICT: Sequential, Serena (fallback not allowed)\n- STANDARD: Sequential, Context7 (fallback allowed)\n- LIGHT: None required (fallback allowed)\n- EXEMPT: None required\n\n**Circuit Breaker Behavior**:\n- If required servers unavailable for STRICT tier, block task execution\n- For other tiers, use fallbacks with noted limitations\n\n## Tool Coordination\n\n**Planning Phase**:\n1. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Grep/Glob: Find references\n3. find_referencing_symbols: Trace dependencies\n\n**Verification Phase**:\n1. Task (quality-engineer): Spawn verification agent (STRICT only)\n2. Bash: Run tests directly (STANDARD)\n3. think_about_task_adherence: Reflect on completeness\n\n**Completion Phase**:\n1. write_memory: Save session state\n2. think_about_whether_you_are_done: Final check\n\n## Examples\n\n### STRICT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"implement user authentication with JWT\"\n\n-> Classified as STRICT (security domain, authentication keyword)\n-> Full 6-category checklist enforced\n-> Verification agent spawned\n-> Adversarial questions answered\n```\n\n### STANDARD Task\n```\n/sc:task \"add pagination to user list\"\n\n-> Classified as STANDARD (add keyword, typical feature)\n-> Context loaded before editing\n-> Downstream impacts checked\n-> Direct test execution\n```\n\n### LIGHT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"fix typo in README\"\n\n-> Classified as LIGHT (trivial classification\n-> Full verification enforced\n```\n\n## Boundaries\n\n**Will:**\n- Classify tasks into appropriate compliance tiers\n- Enforce tier-appropriate verification requirements\n- Provide {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01VnUejo4EBeW3AcFNWTxvy3","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→component: roadmap-pipeline\n     3→framework: IronClaude\n     4→phase: 3\n     5→generated: 2026-03-14\n     6→evidence_source: auggie-mcp\n     7→---\n     8→\n     9→# Strategy: IronClaude Roadmap Pipeline\n    10→\n    11→## 1. Design Philosophy\n    12→\n    13→The roadmap pipeline exists to eliminate LLM output variance when generating project roadmaps from specifications. The core design decision is to treat roadmap generation as a structured, multi-step pipeline with file-on-disk artifacts between steps — rather than a single large prompt — because each artifact acts as both a quality gate input and a resume checkpoint.\n    14→\n    15→**Why this design exists**: A single monolithic roadmap generation prompt has no way to enforce intermediate quality requirements, provides no recovery surface if one step fails, and cannot systematically exploit model diversity (e.g., architect persona vs. analyzer persona producing different variant roadmaps). The 9-step pipeline with parallel generate steps (2a/2b) was chosen explicitly to produce two independently generated variants that are then compared adversarially, which surfaces assumptions and trade-offs that a single generation would suppress.\n    16→\n    17→**Trade-off**: The pipeline introduces significant latency (up to 900s per generate step, 300s per analysis step) and file I/O overhead compared to a direct prompt. Benefit: each step is independently verifiable; HALT diagnostic output identifies exactly which step failed with a human-readable reason.\n    18→\n    19→## 2. Execution Model\n    20→\n    21→The pipeline is built as a declarative list of `Step` objects (and parallel `list[Step]` groups) constructed by `_build_steps(config: RoadmapConfig)` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:302`). Execution is delegated to the shared `execute_pipeline()` function (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/executor.py:46`), which processes steps sequentially, dispatching parallel groups via `_run_parallel_steps()`.\n    22→\n    23→**9-step sequence**:\n    24→1. `extract` — spec decomposition into structured requirements (5-minute timeout)\n    25→2. `generate-<agent_a>` + `generate-<agent_b>` — parallel variant generation (15-minute timeout each)\n    26→3. `diff` — structural and content diff analysis between variants\n    27→4. `debate` — adversarial debate resolving diff points\n    28→5. `score` — hybrid quantitative + qualitative scoring; base selection\n    29→6. `merge` — selected base + planned improvements from non-base variant\n    30→7. `test-strategy` — test plan generation for merged roadmap\n    31→8. `spec-fidelity` — verifies merged roadmap covers all spec requirements\n    32→\n    33→Each step produces a named output file and is validated by `gate_passed(output_file, criteria)` (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/gates.py:20`). Gate tiers: EXEMPT / LIGHT / STANDARD / STRICT, with STRICT adding semantic checks (pure Python, no subprocess).\n    34→\n    35→**State persistence**: `_save_state(config, results)` writes `.roadmap-state.json` after each step. `--resume` re-enters the pipeline at the first step that has not yet passed its gate, via `_apply_resume()` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:1273`).\n    36→\n    37→**Stale spec detection**: `_apply_resume` computes `sha256` of the spec file and compares to `state[\"spec_hash\"]`. If changed, the extract step is forced to re-run even if its gate previously passed (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:1287`).\n    38→\n    39→## 3. Quality Enforcement\n    40→\n    41→Quality is enforced at two levels:\n    42→\n    43→**Per-step gates**: `GateCriteria` specifies `required_frontmatter_fields`, `min_lines`, and optional `semantic_checks`. EXTRACT_GATE, GENERATE_A_GATE, GENERATE_B_GATE, DEBATE_GATE, SCORE_GATE each have tier-appropriate criteria. STRICT gates add `SemanticCheck` lambdas that run against file content without LLM invocation (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/models.py:58`).\n    44→\n    45→**Spec-fidelity gate**: Step 8 (`spec-fidelity`) is gated by SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE and verifies that the merged roadmap references all requirements from the spec file. This step is explicitly noted to NOT be skipped by `--no-validate` — the `--no-validate` flag only skips the post-pipeline validation subsystem, not spec-fidelity itself (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:827`).\n    46→\n    47→**Trade-off**: Gate checks are fast (pure Python) but structurally shallow. A gate can pass a syntactically valid document that is semantically empty. The spec-fidelity step adds LLM-based semantic coverage verification, but that step itself is gated only structurally. This creates a residual risk: a low-quality but structurally valid spec-fidelity report will pass the gate.\n    48→\n    49→## 4. Error Handling Strategy\n    50→\n    51→Failures produce structured HALT output via `_format_halt_output()` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:437`), which lists failed steps (FAIL or TIMEOUT), passed steps, and cancelled (downstream) steps.\n    52→\n    53→**Retry logic**: Each step has `retry_limit=1` (one retry attempt on gate failure) before the pipeline halts. The retry re-executes the same Claude subprocess with the same prompt — it does not modify the prompt.\n    54→\n    55→**Spec-fidelity auto-resume**: If specifically `spec-fidelity` fails and an auto-resume condition is met, the executor can attempt to auto-resume from that step (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:883`). This is a targeted recovery path for the most common late-stage failure mode.\n    56→\n    57→**Trade-off**: Retry with identical prompt is a weak recovery mechanism — if the model produced substandard output once, it may do so again. No prompt adaptation occurs on retry. The benefit is simplicity and reproducibility.\n    58→\n    59→## 5. Extension Points\n    60→\n    61→- **Agent specs**: `--agents model[:persona]` injects arbitrary Claude model/persona pairs into generate steps. Default: `opus:architect` + `haiku:architect` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/models.py:85`).\n    62→- **Depth control**: `--depth quick|standard|deep` alters the debate step's round configuration.\n    63→- **Step list extensibility**: `_build_steps` returns a plain Python list; new steps can be appended without executor changes.\n    64→- **Output directory**: Configurable via `--output`; all artifact paths are derived from `config.output_dir`.\n    65→- **Resume**: `_apply_resume()` and gate checks enable any step to be skipped on re-entry. No step is hard-coded as non-resumable.\n    66→\n    67→## 6. System Qualities\n    68→\n    69→**Maintainability**: The 9-step pipeline is fully explicit and readable in `_build_steps()`. Each step is a simple dataclass with named fields; no implicit control flow. Sprint and roadmap share the same `execute_pipeline()` function, so executor improvements propagate to both consumers.\n    70→\n    71→**Weakness**: Roadmap pipeline is tightly coupled to the specific 9-step sequence. Adding a step requires modifying `_build_steps()` and potentially defining new gate constants. There is no plugin mechanism for step injection at runtime.\n    72→\n    73→**Checkpoint Reliability**: `.roadmap-state.json` persists step pass/fail status per run. `--resume` reads this state and re-checks gate status on disk. Stale spec detection (hash comparison) prevents silently resuming with a changed spec file.\n    74→\n    75→**Weakness**: State file records step IDs as strings. If a step is renamed between runs, resume logic will not recognize the previously-completed step and will re-run it — producing duplicate artifacts.\n    76→\n    77→**Extensibility**: The `AgentSpec` model is open-ended; any model:persona string is accepted. The parallel generate group is structurally a `list[Step]`, so additional agents can be added without executor changes.\n    78→\n    79→**Weakness**: Adding more than 2 generate agents increases latency proportionally (timeout per agent) and potentially degrades downstream diff quality as the diff step scales O(n²) in comparison complexity.\n    80→\n    81→**Operational Determinism**: Gate validation is pure Python. Same file content produces same gate pass/fail result. The scoring algorithm (50% quantitative + 50% qualitative) and tiebreaker protocol produce deterministic base selection for a given set of inputs.\n    82→\n    83→**Weakness**: The generate steps invoke Claude LLM subprocesses whose outputs are inherently non-deterministic. Two runs of the same pipeline with the same inputs will produce different variant roadmaps, and potentially different final merged outputs.\n    84→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Design Philosophy\n\nThe roadmap pipeline exists to eliminate LLM output variance when generating project roadmaps from specifications. The core design decision is to treat roadmap generation as a structured, multi-step pipeline with file-on-disk artifacts between steps — rather than a single large prompt — because each artifact acts as both a quality gate input and a resume checkpoint.\n\n**Why this design exists**: A single monolithic roadmap generation prompt has no way to enforce intermediate quality requirements, provides no recovery surface if one step fails, and cannot systematically exploit model diversity (e.g., architect persona vs. analyzer persona producing different variant roadmaps). The 9-step pipeline with parallel generate steps (2a/2b) was chosen explicitly to produce two independently generated variants that are then compared adversarially, which surfaces assumptions and trade-offs that a single generation would suppress.\n\n**Trade-off**: The pipeline introduces significant latency (up to 900s per generate step, 300s per analysis step) and file I/O overhead compared to a direct prompt. Benefit: each step is independently verifiable; HALT diagnostic output identifies exactly which step failed with a human-readable reason.\n\n## 2. Execution Model\n\nThe pipeline is built as a declarative list of `Step` objects (and parallel `list[Step]` groups) constructed by `_build_steps(config: RoadmapConfig)` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:302`). Execution is delegated to the shared `execute_pipeline()` function (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/executor.py:46`), which processes steps sequentially, dispatching parallel groups via `_run_parallel_steps()`.\n\n**9-step sequence**:\n1. `extract` — spec decomposition into structured requirements (5-minute timeout)\n2. `generate-<agent_a>` + `generate-<agent_b>` — parallel variant generation (15-minute timeout each)\n3. `diff` — structural and content diff analysis between variants\n4. `debate` — adversarial debate resolving diff points\n5. `score` — hybrid quantitative + qualitative scoring; base selection\n6. `merge` — selected base + planned improvements from non-base variant\n7. `test-strategy` — test plan generation for merged roadmap\n8. `spec-fidelity` — verifies merged roadmap covers all spec requirements\n\nEach step produces a named output file and is validated by `gate_passed(output_file, criteria)` (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/gates.py:20`). Gate tiers: EXEMPT / LIGHT / STANDARD / STRICT, with STRICT adding semantic checks (pure Python, no subprocess).\n\n**State persistence**: `_save_state(config, results)` writes `.roadmap-state.json` after each step. `--resume` re-enters the pipeline at the first step that has not yet passed its gate, via `_apply_resume()` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:1273`).\n\n**Stale spec detection**: `_apply_resume` computes `sha256` of the spec file and compares to `state[\"spec_hash\"]`. If changed, the extract step is forced to re-run even if its gate previously passed (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:1287`).\n\n## 3. Quality Enforcement\n\nQuality is enforced at two levels:\n\n**Per-step gates**: `GateCriteria` specifies `required_frontmatter_fields`, `min_lines`, and optional `semantic_checks`. EXTRACT_GATE, GENERATE_A_GATE, GENERATE_B_GATE, DEBATE_GATE, SCORE_GATE each have tier-appropriate criteria. STRICT gates add `SemanticCheck` lambdas that run against file content without LLM invocation (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/models.py:58`).\n\n**Spec-fidelity gate**: Step 8 (`spec-fidelity`) is gated by SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE and verifies that the merged roadmap references all requirements from the spec file. This step is explicitly noted to NOT be skipped by `--no-validate` — the `--no-validate` flag only skips the post-pipeline validation subsystem, not spec-fidelity itself (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:827`).\n\n**Trade-off**: Gate checks are fast (pure Python) but structurally shallow. A gate can pass a syntactically valid document that is semantically empty. The spec-fidelity step adds LLM-based semantic coverage verification, but that step itself is gated only structurally. This creates a residual risk: a low-quality but structurally valid spec-fidelity report will pass the gate.\n\n## 4. Error Handling Strategy\n\nFailures produce structured HALT output via `_format_halt_output()` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:437`), which lists failed steps (FAIL or TIMEOUT), passed steps, and cancelled (downstream) steps.\n\n**Retry logic**: Each step has `retry_limit=1` (one retry attempt on gate failure) before the pipeline halts. The retry re-executes the same Claude subprocess with the same prompt — it does not modify the prompt.\n\n**Spec-fidelity auto-resume**: If specifically `spec-fidelity` fails and an auto-resume condition is met, the executor can attempt to auto-resume from that step (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/executor.py:883`). This is a targeted recovery path for the most common late-stage failure mode.\n\n**Trade-off**: Retry with identical prompt is a weak recovery mechanism — if the model produced substandard output once, it may do so again. No prompt adaptation occurs on retry. The benefit is simplicity and reproducibility.\n\n## 5. Extension Points\n\n- **Agent specs**: `--agents model[:persona]` injects arbitrary Claude model/persona pairs into generate steps. Default: `opus:architect` + `haiku:architect` (`src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/models.py:85`).\n- **Depth control**: `--depth quick|standard|deep` alters the debate step's round configuration.\n- **Step list extensibility**: `_build_steps` returns a plain Python list; new steps can be appended without executor changes.\n- **Output directory**: Configurable via `--output`; all artifact paths are derived from `config.output_dir`.\n- **Resume**: `_apply_resume()` and gate checks enable any step to be skipped on re-entry. No step is hard-coded as non-resumable.\n\n## 6. System Qualities\n\n**Maintainability**: The 9-step pipeline is fully explicit and readable in `_build_steps()`. Each step is a simple dataclass with named fields; no implicit control flow. Sprint and roadmap share the same `execute_pipeline()` function, so executor improvements propagate to both consumers.\n\n**Weakness**: Roadmap pipeline is tightly coupled to the specific 9-step sequence. Adding a step requires modifying `_build_steps()` and potentially defining new gate constants. There is no plugin mechanism for step injection at runtime.\n\n**Checkpoint Reliability**: `.roadmap-state.json` persists step pass/fail status per run. `--resume` reads this state and re-checks gate status on disk. Stale spec detection (hash comparison) prevents silently resuming with a changed spec file.\n\n**Weakness**: State file records step IDs as strings. If a step is renamed between runs, resume logic will not recognize the previously-completed step and will re-run it — producing duplicate artifacts.\n\n**Extensibility**: The `AgentSpec` model is open-ended; any model:persona string is accepted. The parallel generate group is structurally a `list[Step]`, so additional agents can be added without executor changes.\n\n**Weakness**: Adding more than 2 generate agents increases latency proportionally (timeout per agent) and potentially degrades downstream diff quality as the diff step scales O(n²) in comparison complexity.\n\n**Operational Determinism**: Gate validation is pure Python. Same file content produces same gate pass/fail result. The scoring algorithm (50% quantitative + 50% qualitative) and tiebreaker protocol produce deterministic base selection for a given set of inputs.\n\n**Weakness**: The generate steps invoke Claude LLM subprocesses whose outputs are inherently non-deterministic. Two runs of the same pipeline with the same inputs will produce different variant roadmaps, and potentially different final merged outputs.\n","numLines":84,"startLine":1,"totalLines":84}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01UPZmigDxbPj1g3fACE8AiZ","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→component: sprint-executor\n     3→framework: IronClaude\n     4→phase: 3\n     5→generated: 2026-03-14\n     6→evidence_source: auggie-mcp\n     7→---\n     8→\n     9→# Strategy: IronClaude Sprint Executor\n    10→\n    11→## 1. Design Philosophy\n    12→\n    13→The sprint executor exists to run multi-phase, multi-task Claude agent workflows from declarative tasklist files, with deterministic phase-level checkpointing and budget control. The design philosophy centers on **supervised orchestration**: the executor is a thin Python supervisor that manages subprocess lifecycle, output monitoring, gate evaluation, and budget accounting — while delegating all task-level reasoning to Claude subprocess instances.\n    14→\n    15→**Why this design exists**: Running complex multi-task agent workflows directly as a single Claude session creates token budget exhaustion, loss of intermediate progress on failure, and no mechanism for human review between phases. The sprint executor decouples the orchestrator (Python supervisor) from the agent (Claude subprocess) to enable: phase-level restart (`--start N`), budget-tracked multi-task execution, and observable progress via TUI and logging.\n    16→\n    17→**Trade-off**: The supervisor model introduces subprocess spawn overhead per phase and constrains task execution to one subprocess per phase. A single Claude subprocess handles all tasks in a phase sequentially, which means a long-running task in Phase 2 blocks all subsequent Phase 2 tasks. The benefit is simplicity in the supervisor loop and clean phase-level isolation.\n    18→\n    19→## 2. Execution Model\n    20→\n    21→`execute_sprint(config: SprintConfig)` (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/executor.py:490`) implements the main orchestration loop:\n    22→\n    23→For each active phase:\n    24→1. Spawn `ClaudeProcess(config, phase)` — a sprint-specific subprocess (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/process.py:88`)\n    25→2. Start `OutputMonitor` thread tracking output byte growth\n    26→3. Poll TUI in a monotonic-clock timeout loop\n    27→4. On process exit, parse result file for CONTINUE/HALT signal\n    28→5. Record `PhaseResult`; decide whether to proceed or halt\n    29→\n    30→**ClaudeProcess**: Extends `_PipelineClaudeProcess` with sprint-specific prompt builder (`build_prompt()`) and lifecycle hooks (spawn, signal, exit) wired via factory closures. Timeout is computed as `max_turns * 120 + 300` seconds — a linear function of turn budget ensuring timeout scales with expected workload (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/process.py:108`).\n    31→\n    32→**TurnLedger**: `execute_phase_tasks()` (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/executor.py:349`) uses `TurnLedger` for budget allocation across tasks in a phase. Ledger enforces monotonicity (consumed can only increase), tracks reimbursement at 80% rate for PASS tasks, and enforces `minimum_allocation=5` turns before launching a subprocess (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/models.py:466`). Tasks below minimum allocation are skipped and logged as remaining.\n    33→\n    34→**Phase discovery**: `load_sprint_config()` (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/config.py:104`) discovers phase files matching `PHASE_FILE_PATTERN` regex — supporting 4 canonical filename conventions (e.g., `phase-1-tasklist.md`, `p1-tasklist.md`). Phase range filtering via `--start` / `--end` produces `config.active_phases`.\n    35→\n    36→**Tmux integration**: By default, sprint launches inside a tmux session for SSH-disconnect resilience. `launch_in_tmux()` re-launches the sprint command inside a named tmux session; `update_tail_pane()` tails output to a tmux split pane.\n    37→\n    38→## 3. Quality Enforcement\n    39→\n    40→**Gate validation**: After each phase, `gate_passed(output_file, criteria)` (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/gates.py:20`) validates the phase output file against tier-proportional criteria. STRICT gates include semantic checks (pure Python lambdas). Gate failure triggers HALT unless `--shadow-gates` is active.\n    41→\n    42→**Shadow gate mode**: `--shadow-gates` runs `TrailingGateRunner` (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/trailing_gate.py`) as a daemon thread — gates execute asynchronously without blocking the main executor loop. Failures are logged as metrics-only warnings, not execution halts. This allows pipeline progress monitoring without enforcement during development or debugging.\n    43→\n    44→**Stall detection**: `detect_error_max_turns()` and byte-growth monitoring in `OutputMonitor` detect processes that have stopped producing output. `stall_timeout` + `stall_action` (kill/warn) provide configurable watchdog behavior.\n    45→\n    46→**Trade-off**: Shadow gates trade safety for observability — pipelines can proceed past failing gates, accumulating invalid artifacts. This is appropriate for development but must never be used in production sprint runs where downstream tasks depend on upstream gate outputs.\n    47→\n    48→## 4. Error Handling Strategy\n    49→\n    50→**Phase-level HALT**: If `gate_passed()` returns `(False, reason)` and retries are exhausted, the sprint halts at that phase. All results up to that point are written to `results/` dir on disk. `--start N` allows re-entry from the halted phase after human intervention.\n    51→\n    52→**Signal handling**: `SignalHandler` installs SIGINT/SIGTERM handlers. On signal, `shutdown_requested = True` is set; the executor cleans up the active subprocess and writes `INTERRUPTED` outcome before exiting.\n    53→\n    54→**Budget exhaustion**: If `TurnLedger.available()` falls below `minimum_allocation`, remaining tasks are returned as unattempted. The executor logs which tasks were skipped and records budget exhaustion in the phase result.\n    55→\n    56→**Diagnostic chain**: On failure, the 4-stage diagnostic chain (`run_diagnostic_chain()`) can be triggered: troubleshoot → adversarial analysis × 2 → summary. This is runner-side and does not consume TurnLedger turns (diagnostic invocations are not billed against task budget per spec Gap 2).\n    57→\n    58→**Trade-off**: Phase-level granularity for `--start` restart means that if a phase completes 9 tasks and fails on task 10, all 10 tasks must re-run on restart (the executor cannot resume mid-phase). Intra-phase checkpoint granularity is not supported.\n    59→\n    60→## 5. Extension Points\n    61→\n    62→- `--start` / `--end` phase range — limit execution to a subset of phases without modifying the tasklist.\n    63→- `--shadow-gates` — decouple gate evaluation from execution blocking.\n    64→- `stall_timeout` + `stall_action` — configurable watchdog per deployment environment.\n    65→- `_subprocess_factory` parameter on `execute_phase_tasks` — injectable for test-time subprocess substitution without modifying executor code (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/executor.py:356`).\n    66→- `TrailingGatePolicy` injectable on sprint executor — allows custom gate evaluation policies per consumer (T07.01 design).\n    67→- `--no-tmux` flag — disable tmux wrapping for environments where tmux is unavailable.\n    68→\n    69→## 6. System Qualities\n    70→\n    71→**Maintainability**: Sprint and roadmap share the same `execute_pipeline()` function and `ClaudeProcess` base class. Changes to the generic executor benefit both consumers. The sprint-specific `execute_sprint()` is a thin loop over `execute_phase_tasks()` with TUI and logging decorators.\n    72→\n    73→**Weakness**: The supervisor loop is monolithic — TUI polling, timeout enforcement, and gate evaluation are all in the same polling loop. Extracting these concerns independently would improve testability and allow alternative frontends (e.g., headless CI mode).\n    74→\n    75→**Checkpoint Reliability**: Phase results are written to `results/` dir after each phase completes. `--start N` enables phase-level re-entry. TurnLedger state is not persisted to disk — if the supervisor is killed mid-phase, budget consumption tracking is lost and must be re-estimated on restart.\n    76→\n    77→**Weakness**: No intra-phase checkpoint. A phase with many tasks that crashes at task N requires re-running tasks 1 through N-1, consuming turn budget and time.\n    78→\n    79→**Extensibility**: `TrailingGatePolicy` and `_subprocess_factory` injection points make the executor testable and consumer-adaptable. Phase discovery via regex supports 4 filename conventions, accommodating different project naming styles.\n    80→\n    81→**Weakness**: Phase discovery regex is hard-coded. Projects using non-canonical naming conventions (e.g., `sprint-phase-3.md`) require modifying `PHASE_FILE_PATTERN`.\n    82→\n    83→**Operational Determinism**: Gate tiers (EXEMPT/LIGHT/STANDARD/STRICT) produce deterministic pass/fail for a given output file and criteria. Turn budget arithmetic is pure Python with no floating-point ambiguity (integer arithmetic). Monotonic clock (`time.monotonic()`) for deadline enforcement prevents NTP adjustment interference.\n    84→\n    85→**Weakness**: Phase execution order depends on the filesystem sort order of discovered phase files. Phases with the same number prefix from different naming conventions could collide in ordering; the regex captures only the first matched number group.\n    86→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2a8973e7-df48-425c-933b-70e9c14aab0b","uuid":"7586a1df-0ce8-4c71-a7d9-b16ff0597433","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/config/workspace/IronClaude/.dev/releases/current/cross-framework-deep-analysis/artifacts/strategy-ic-sprint-executor.md","content":"---\ncomponent: sprint-executor\nframework: IronClaude\nphase: 3\ngenerated: 2026-03-14\nevidence_source: auggie-mcp\n---\n\n# Strategy: IronClaude Sprint Executor\n\n## 1. Design Philosophy\n\nThe sprint executor exists to run multi-phase, multi-task Claude agent workflows from declarative tasklist files, with deterministic phase-level checkpointing and budget control. The design philosophy centers on **supervised orchestration**: the executor is a thin Python supervisor that manages subprocess lifecycle, output monitoring, gate evaluation, and budget accounting — while delegating all task-level reasoning to Claude subprocess instances.\n\n**Why this design exists**: Running complex multi-task agent workflows directly as a single Claude session creates token budget exhaustion, loss of intermediate progress on failure, and no mechanism for human review between phases. The sprint executor decouples the orchestrator (Python supervisor) from the agent (Claude subprocess) to enable: phase-level restart (`--start N`), budget-tracked multi-task execution, and observable progress via TUI and logging.\n\n**Trade-off**: The supervisor model introduces subprocess spawn overhead per phase and constrains task execution to one subprocess per phase. A single Claude subprocess handles all tasks in a phase sequentially, which means a long-running task in Phase 2 blocks all subsequent Phase 2 tasks. The benefit is simplicity in the supervisor loop and clean phase-level isolation.\n\n## 2. Execution Model\n\n`execute_sprint(config: SprintConfig)` (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/executor.py:490`) implements the main orchestration loop:\n\nFor each active phase:\n1. Spawn `ClaudeProcess(config, phase)` — a sprint-specific subprocess (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/process.py:88`)\n2. Start `OutputMonitor` thread tracking output byte growth\n3. Poll TUI in a monotonic-clock timeout loop\n4. On process exit, parse result file for CONTINUE/HALT signal\n5. Record `PhaseResult`; decide whether to proceed or halt\n\n**ClaudeProcess**: Extends `_PipelineClaudeProcess` with sprint-specific prompt builder (`build_prompt()`) and lifecycle hooks (spawn, signal, exit) wired via factory closures. Timeout is computed as `max_turns * 120 + 300` seconds — a linear function of turn budget ensuring timeout scales with expected workload (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/process.py:108`).\n\n**TurnLedger**: `execute_phase_tasks()` (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/executor.py:349`) uses `TurnLedger` for budget allocation across tasks in a phase. Ledger enforces monotonicity (consumed can only increase), tracks reimbursement at 80% rate for PASS tasks, and enforces `minimum_allocation=5` turns before launching a subprocess (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/models.py:466`). Tasks below minimum allocation are skipped and logged as remaining.\n\n**Phase discovery**: `load_sprint_config()` (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/config.py:104`) discovers phase files matching `PHASE_FILE_PATTERN` regex — supporting 4 canonical filename conventions (e.g., `phase-1-tasklist.md`, `p1-tasklist.md`). Phase range filtering via `--start` / `--end` produces `config.active_phases`.\n\n**Tmux integration**: By default, sprint launches inside a tmux session for SSH-disconnect resilience. `launch_in_tmux()` re-launches the sprint command inside a named tmux session; `update_tail_pane()` tails output to a tmux split pane.\n\n## 3. Quality Enforcement\n\n**Gate validation**: After each phase, `gate_passed(output_file, criteria)` (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/gates.py:20`) validates the phase output file against tier-proportional criteria. STRICT gates include semantic checks (pure Python lambdas). Gate failure triggers HALT unless `--shadow-gates` is active.\n\n**Shadow gate mode**: `--shadow-gates` runs `TrailingGateRunner` (`src/superclaude/cli/pipeline/trailing_gate.py`) as a daemon thread — gates execute asynchronously without blocking the main executor loop. Failures are logged as metrics-only warnings, not execution halts. This allows pipeline progress monitoring without enforcement during development or debugging.\n\n**Stall detection**: `detect_error_max_turns()` and byte-growth monitoring in `OutputMonitor` detect processes that have stopped producing output. `stall_timeout` + `stall_action` (kill/warn) provide configurable watchdog behavior.\n\n**Trade-off**: Shadow gates trade safety for observability — pipelines can proceed past failing gates, accumulating invalid artifacts. This is appropriate for development but must never be used in production sprint runs where downstream tasks depend on upstream gate outputs.\n\n## 4. Error Handling Strategy\n\n**Phase-level HALT**: If `gate_passed()` returns `(False, reason)` and retries are exhausted, the sprint halts at that phase. All results up to that point are written to `results/` dir on disk. `--start N` allows re-entry from the halted phase after human intervention.\n\n**Signal handling**: `SignalHandler` installs SIGINT/SIGTERM handlers. On signal, `shutdown_requested = True` is set; the executor cleans up the active subprocess and writes `INTERRUPTED` outcome before exiting.\n\n**Budget exhaustion**: If `TurnLedger.available()` falls below `minimum_allocation`, remaining tasks are returned as unattempted. The executor logs which tasks were skipped and records budget exhaustion in the phase result.\n\n**Diagnostic chain**: On failure, the 4-stage diagnostic chain (`run_diagnostic_chain()`) can be triggered: troubleshoot → adversarial analysis × 2 → summary. This is runner-side and does not consume TurnLedger turns (diagnostic invocations are not billed against task budget per spec Gap 2).\n\n**Trade-off**: Phase-level granularity for `--start` restart means that if a phase completes 9 tasks and fails on task 10, all 10 tasks must re-run on restart (the executor cannot resume mid-phase). Intra-phase checkpoint granularity is not supported.\n\n## 5. Extension Points\n\n- `--start` / `--end` phase range — limit execution to a subset of phases without modifying the tasklist.\n- `--shadow-gates` — decouple gate evaluation from execution blocking.\n- `stall_timeout` + `stall_action` — configurable watchdog per deployment environment.\n- `_subprocess_factory` parameter on `execute_phase_tasks` — injectable for test-time subprocess substitution without modifying executor code (`src/superclaude/cli/sprint/executor.py:356`).\n- `TrailingGatePolicy` injectable on sprint executor — allows custom gate evaluation policies per consumer (T07.01 design).\n- `--no-tmux` flag — disable tmux wrapping for environments where tmux is unavailable.\n\n## 6. System Qualities\n\n**Maintainability**: Sprint and roadmap share the same `execute_pipeline()` function and `ClaudeProcess` base class. Changes to the generic executor benefit both consumers. The sprint-specific `execute_sprint()` is a thin loop over `execute_phase_tasks()` with TUI and logging decorators.\n\n**Weakness**: The supervisor loop is monolithic — TUI polling, timeout enforcement, and gate evaluation are all in the same polling loop. Extracting these concerns independently would improve testability and allow alternative frontends (e.g., headless CI mode).\n\n**Checkpoint Reliability**: Phase results are written to `results/` dir after each phase completes. `--start N` enables phase-level re-entry. TurnLedger state is not persisted to disk — if the supervisor is killed mid-phase, budget consumption tracking is lost and must be re-estimated on restart.\n\n**Weakness**: No intra-phase checkpoint. A phase with many tasks that crashes at task N requires re-running tasks 1 through N-1, consuming turn budget and time.\n\n**Extensibility**: `TrailingGatePolicy` and `_subprocess_factory` injection points make the executor testable and consumer-adaptable. Phase discovery via regex supports 4 filename conventions, accommodating different project naming styles.\n\n**Weakness**: Phase discovery regex is hard-coded. Projects using non-canonical naming conventions (e.g., `sprint-phase-3.md`) require modifying `PHASE_FILE_PATTERN`.\n\n**Operational Determinism**: Gate tiers (EXEMPT/LIGHT/STANDARD/STRICT) produce deterministic pass/fail for a given output file and criteria. Turn budget arithmetic is pure Python with no floating-point ambiguity (integer arithmetic). Monotonic clock (`time.monotonic()`) for deadline enforcement prevents NTP adjustment interference.\n\n**Weakness**: Phase execution order depends on the filesystem sort order of discovered phase files. Phases with the same number prefix from different naming conventions could collide in ordering; the regex captures only the first matched number group.\n","numLines":86,"startLine":1,"totalLines":86}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01HX576sc98tvUfGNCLM9mFq","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→component: pm-agent\n     3→framework: IronClaude\n     4→phase: 3\n     5→generated: 2026-03-14\n     6→evidence_source: auggie-mcp\n     7→---\n     8→\n     9→# Strategy: IronClaude PM Agent\n    10→\n    11→## 1. Design Philosophy\n    12→\n    13→The PM Agent exists to reduce wrong-direction work and post-implementation rework through three orthogonal quality patterns: pre-execution confidence gating, post-implementation evidence validation, and cross-session error learning. The core design decision is to implement these as **importable Python classes** rather than pure Markdown behavioral prompts, enabling testability via pytest fixtures and programmatic integration.\n    14→\n    15→**Why this design exists**: The original SuperClaude skill system placed PM Agent behavior in a Markdown SKILL.md file, requiring full file reads (35K–40K tokens) and relying on Claude to follow the behavioral protocol without verification. The Python implementation (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/`) makes each pattern independently testable, composable via pytest fixtures (`src/superclaude/pytest_plugin.py:1`), and token-efficient (pre-execution check costs 100–200 tokens vs. 5K–50K tokens of incorrect implementation).\n    16→\n    17→**Trade-off**: The Python-based patterns require a pip-installed `superclaude` package, creating a deployment dependency. The Markdown agent definition (`.claude/agents/pm-agent.md`) remains as a complementary layer for Claude Code integration, creating dual representations of the same behavioral protocol that must be kept synchronized.\n    18→\n    19→## 2. Execution Model\n    20→\n    21→The PM Agent operates as a meta-layer above specialist agents, with three distinct trigger paths:\n    22→\n    23→**Path 1 — Pre-execution (ConfidenceChecker)**:\n    24→`ConfidenceChecker.assess(context: dict) -> float` (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/confidence.py:42`) runs 5 weighted checks:\n    25→1. No duplicate implementations (25%) — `_no_duplicates(context)`\n    26→2. Architecture compliance (25%) — `_architecture_compliant(context)`\n    27→3. Official documentation verified (20%) — `_has_official_docs(context)`\n    28→4. Working OSS implementations referenced (15%) — `_has_oss_reference(context)`\n    29→5. Root cause identified (15%) — `_root_cause_identified(context)`\n    30→\n    31→Score thresholds: ≥0.90 → proceed; 0.70–0.89 → present alternatives; <0.70 → stop and ask.\n    32→\n    33→**Path 2 — Post-implementation (SelfCheckProtocol)**:\n    34→`SelfCheckProtocol.validate(implementation: dict) -> (bool, list[str])` (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/self_check.py:64`) runs 4 mandatory questions: tests passing with evidence, requirements met, assumptions verified, evidence provided. Additionally detects 7 hallucination red flags including uncertainty language (`probably`, `maybe`, `should work`) and \"complete\" status with failing tests (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/self_check.py:212`).\n    35→\n    36→**Path 3 — Error learning (ReflexionPattern)**:\n    37→`ReflexionPattern.get_solution(error_info) -> Optional[dict]` (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/reflexion.py:76`) performs smart lookup using Mindbase semantic search (primary) or grep-based text search (fallback) against `docs/memory/solutions_learned.jsonl`. Cache hit returns known solution at 0 tokens; cache miss triggers investigation and `record_error()` persists the new solution to dual storage (JSONL + Mindbase).\n    38→\n    39→**Token budget**: `TokenBudgetManager.LIMITS = {simple: 200, medium: 1000, complex: 2500}` — static constants ensuring deterministic allocation (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/token_budget.py:17`).\n    40→\n    41→**Pytest integration**: Auto-loaded via `pyproject.toml` `entry-points.pytest11`. Fixtures (`confidence_checker`, `self_check_protocol`, `reflexion_pattern`, `token_budget`, `pm_context`) are available without explicit import in any test that installs the package (`src/superclaude/pytest_plugin.py:1`).\n    42→\n    43→## 3. Quality Enforcement\n    44→\n    45→**Pre-execution gate**: The 90% confidence threshold enforces that implementation cannot begin until sufficient context has been gathered. Reported ROI: 25–250x token savings (spending 100–200 tokens on confidence check to save 5K–50K tokens of misdirected work).\n    46→\n    47→**Post-implementation anti-hallucination**: The 7 red-flag detection in `SelfCheckProtocol._detect_hallucinations()` specifically targets LLM failure modes: claims without evidence, complete status with failing tests, uncertainty language in descriptions, ignored errors/warnings.\n    48→\n    49→**Error recurrence prevention**: `ReflexionPattern` targets <10% error recurrence rate via solution reuse rate >90%. Cache hits cost 0 tokens and return immediately, making this the lowest-cost quality gate in the system.\n    50→\n    51→**Trade-off**: The `_architecture_compliant()` and `_root_cause_identified()` methods in `ConfidenceChecker` are documented as placeholder implementations (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/confidence.py:162`). They check for specific dict keys (`architecture_check_complete`, etc.) rather than performing actual architectural analysis. This means a caller that sets these keys to `True` without doing real checks can bypass the confidence gate.\n    52→\n    53→## 4. Error Handling Strategy\n    54→\n    55→**STOP-and-ask protocol**: Confidence <0.70 triggers an explicit stop — the pattern is designed to halt work, not to proceed with low confidence. This is enforced behaviorally (via the pm-agent.md agent definition) but not enforced programmatically (the Python class returns a score; the caller decides what to do with it).\n    56→\n    57→**Dual storage fallback**: ReflexionPattern primary storage (Mindbase) failing falls back to grep-based text search on the JSONL file, then to `None` (no solution found). Fallback to `None` triggers investigation, not failure — the pattern degrades gracefully by discovering root cause rather than blocking work.\n    58→\n    59→**Session persistence**: JSONL storage (`docs/memory/solutions_learned.jsonl`) survives session resets. Serena MCP provides additional session memory for the pm-agent.md agent definition layer.\n    60→\n    61→**Trade-off**: JSONL-based error storage is not deduplicated automatically. Over time, the solutions file may accumulate similar entries with different wording. The Mindbase semantic search mitigates this by matching semantically similar errors, but the JSONL file itself grows unboundedly.\n    62→\n    63→## 5. Extension Points\n    64→\n    65→- `ReflexionPattern(memory_dir=)` — configurable storage path per project or per session.\n    66→- `TokenBudgetManager(complexity='simple|medium|complex')` — three budget levels for different task complexity.\n    67→- `SelfCorrectionEngine(repo_path=)` — configurable repo root for correction context.\n    68→- pytest plugin auto-loading via `entry-points.pytest11` — zero-configuration fixture availability after package install.\n    69→- Placeholder methods (`_architecture_compliant`, `_root_cause_identified`) in `ConfidenceChecker` are explicitly designed for extension — the docstrings specify what a real implementation should do.\n    70→\n    71→## 6. System Qualities\n    72→\n    73→**Maintainability**: Three orthogonal patterns (confidence, self-check, reflexion) are independently usable. No pattern depends on another's implementation. Each is a single Python class with a clearly scoped responsibility.\n    74→\n    75→**Weakness**: The pm-agent.md agent definition and the Python implementation represent the same behavioral protocol in two different formats. Changes to one do not automatically propagate to the other. A developer could update the Markdown behavioral spec without updating the Python implementation, or vice versa, silently diverging the two.\n    76→\n    77→**Checkpoint Reliability**: Error solutions persist to JSONL and survive session reset. This is the only PM Agent data that crosses session boundaries automatically. ConfidenceChecker and SelfCheckProtocol results are ephemeral — they exist only for the duration of a single session.\n    78→\n    79→**Extensibility**: The three patterns are designed for independent extension. The placeholder methods in ConfidenceChecker identify exactly where real implementation is expected. The pytest plugin auto-loading mechanism enables new fixtures to be added without test file changes.\n    80→\n    81→**Weakness**: The current `assess()` implementation treats `_architecture_compliant()` and similar checks as boolean flags in the context dict. Real architectural compliance checking (e.g., verifying that a proposed solution uses the project's existing tech stack) requires integration with project analysis tools that are not yet implemented.\n    82→\n    83→**Operational Determinism**: `TokenBudgetManager.LIMITS` are static constants — deterministic allocation for a given complexity level. `classify_finding()` in the classification engine is deterministic. However, the Mindbase semantic search used in `get_solution()` may return different matches on different runs if the index has been updated between sessions.\n    84→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2a8973e7-df48-425c-933b-70e9c14aab0b","uuid":"0b5581c5-f97d-4089-8a3b-4f80c6e75fe2","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/config/workspace/IronClaude/.dev/releases/current/cross-framework-deep-analysis/artifacts/strategy-ic-pm-agent.md","content":"---\ncomponent: pm-agent\nframework: IronClaude\nphase: 3\ngenerated: 2026-03-14\nevidence_source: auggie-mcp\n---\n\n# Strategy: IronClaude PM Agent\n\n## 1. Design Philosophy\n\nThe PM Agent exists to reduce wrong-direction work and post-implementation rework through three orthogonal quality patterns: pre-execution confidence gating, post-implementation evidence validation, and cross-session error learning. The core design decision is to implement these as **importable Python classes** rather than pure Markdown behavioral prompts, enabling testability via pytest fixtures and programmatic integration.\n\n**Why this design exists**: The original SuperClaude skill system placed PM Agent behavior in a Markdown SKILL.md file, requiring full file reads (35K–40K tokens) and relying on Claude to follow the behavioral protocol without verification. The Python implementation (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/`) makes each pattern independently testable, composable via pytest fixtures (`src/superclaude/pytest_plugin.py:1`), and token-efficient (pre-execution check costs 100–200 tokens vs. 5K–50K tokens of incorrect implementation).\n\n**Trade-off**: The Python-based patterns require a pip-installed `superclaude` package, creating a deployment dependency. The Markdown agent definition (`.claude/agents/pm-agent.md`) remains as a complementary layer for Claude Code integration, creating dual representations of the same behavioral protocol that must be kept synchronized.\n\n## 2. Execution Model\n\nThe PM Agent operates as a meta-layer above specialist agents, with three distinct trigger paths:\n\n**Path 1 — Pre-execution (ConfidenceChecker)**:\n`ConfidenceChecker.assess(context: dict) -> float` (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/confidence.py:42`) runs 5 weighted checks:\n1. No duplicate implementations (25%) — `_no_duplicates(context)`\n2. Architecture compliance (25%) — `_architecture_compliant(context)`\n3. Official documentation verified (20%) — `_has_official_docs(context)`\n4. Working OSS implementations referenced (15%) — `_has_oss_reference(context)`\n5. Root cause identified (15%) — `_root_cause_identified(context)`\n\nScore thresholds: ≥0.90 → proceed; 0.70–0.89 → present alternatives; <0.70 → stop and ask.\n\n**Path 2 — Post-implementation (SelfCheckProtocol)**:\n`SelfCheckProtocol.validate(implementation: dict) -> (bool, list[str])` (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/self_check.py:64`) runs 4 mandatory questions: tests passing with evidence, requirements met, assumptions verified, evidence provided. Additionally detects 7 hallucination red flags including uncertainty language (`probably`, `maybe`, `should work`) and \"complete\" status with failing tests (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/self_check.py:212`).\n\n**Path 3 — Error learning (ReflexionPattern)**:\n`ReflexionPattern.get_solution(error_info) -> Optional[dict]` (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/reflexion.py:76`) performs smart lookup using Mindbase semantic search (primary) or grep-based text search (fallback) against `docs/memory/solutions_learned.jsonl`. Cache hit returns known solution at 0 tokens; cache miss triggers investigation and `record_error()` persists the new solution to dual storage (JSONL + Mindbase).\n\n**Token budget**: `TokenBudgetManager.LIMITS = {simple: 200, medium: 1000, complex: 2500}` — static constants ensuring deterministic allocation (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/token_budget.py:17`).\n\n**Pytest integration**: Auto-loaded via `pyproject.toml` `entry-points.pytest11`. Fixtures (`confidence_checker`, `self_check_protocol`, `reflexion_pattern`, `token_budget`, `pm_context`) are available without explicit import in any test that installs the package (`src/superclaude/pytest_plugin.py:1`).\n\n## 3. Quality Enforcement\n\n**Pre-execution gate**: The 90% confidence threshold enforces that implementation cannot begin until sufficient context has been gathered. Reported ROI: 25–250x token savings (spending 100–200 tokens on confidence check to save 5K–50K tokens of misdirected work).\n\n**Post-implementation anti-hallucination**: The 7 red-flag detection in `SelfCheckProtocol._detect_hallucinations()` specifically targets LLM failure modes: claims without evidence, complete status with failing tests, uncertainty language in descriptions, ignored errors/warnings.\n\n**Error recurrence prevention**: `ReflexionPattern` targets <10% error recurrence rate via solution reuse rate >90%. Cache hits cost 0 tokens and return immediately, making this the lowest-cost quality gate in the system.\n\n**Trade-off**: The `_architecture_compliant()` and `_root_cause_identified()` methods in `ConfidenceChecker` are documented as placeholder implementations (`src/superclaude/pm_agent/confidence.py:162`). They check for specific dict keys (`architecture_check_complete`, etc.) rather than performing actual architectural analysis. This means a caller that sets these keys to `True` without doing real checks can bypass the confidence gate.\n\n## 4. Error Handling Strategy\n\n**STOP-and-ask protocol**: Confidence <0.70 triggers an explicit stop — the pattern is designed to halt work, not to proceed with low confidence. This is enforced behaviorally (via the pm-agent.md agent definition) but not enforced programmatically (the Python class returns a score; the caller decides what to do with it).\n\n**Dual storage fallback**: ReflexionPattern primary storage (Mindbase) failing falls back to grep-based text search on the JSONL file, then to `None` (no solution found). Fallback to `None` triggers investigation, not failure — the pattern degrades gracefully by discovering root cause rather than blocking work.\n\n**Session persistence**: JSONL storage (`docs/memory/solutions_learned.jsonl`) survives session resets. Serena MCP provides additional session memory for the pm-agent.md agent definition layer.\n\n**Trade-off**: JSONL-based error storage is not deduplicated automatically. Over time, the solutions file may accumulate similar entries with different wording. The Mindbase semantic search mitigates this by matching semantically similar errors, but the JSONL file itself grows unboundedly.\n\n## 5. Extension Points\n\n- `ReflexionPattern(memory_dir=)` — configurable storage path per project or per session.\n- `TokenBudgetManager(complexity='simple|medium|complex')` — three budget levels for different task complexity.\n- `SelfCorrectionEngine(repo_path=)` — configurable repo root for correction context.\n- pytest plugin auto-loading via `entry-points.pytest11` — zero-configuration fixture availability after package install.\n- Placeholder methods (`_architecture_compliant`, `_root_cause_identified`) in `ConfidenceChecker` are explicitly designed for extension — the docstrings specify what a real implementation should do.\n\n## 6. System Qualities\n\n**Maintainability**: Three orthogonal patterns (confidence, self-check, reflexion) are independently usable. No pattern depends on another's implementation. Each is a single Python class with a clearly scoped responsibility.\n\n**Weakness**: The pm-agent.md agent definition and the Python implementation represent the same behavioral protocol in two different formats. Changes to one do not automatically propagate to the other. A developer could update the Markdown behavioral spec without updating the Python implementation, or vice versa, silently diverging the two.\n\n**Checkpoint Reliability**: Error solutions persist to JSONL and survive session reset. This is the only PM Agent data that crosses session boundaries automatically. ConfidenceChecker and SelfCheckProtocol results are ephemeral — they exist only for the duration of a single session.\n\n**Extensibility**: The three patterns are designed for independent extension. The placeholder methods in ConfidenceChecker identify exactly where real implementation is expected. The pytest plugin auto-loading mechanism enables new fixtures to be added without test file changes.\n\n**Weakness**: The current `assess()` implementation treats `_architecture_compliant()` and similar checks as boolean flags in the context dict. Real architectural compliance checking (e.g., verifying that a proposed solution uses the project's existing tech stack) requires integration with project analysis tools that are not yet implemented.\n\n**Operational Determinism**: `TokenBudgetManager.LIMITS` are static constants — deterministic allocation for a given complexity level. `classify_finding()` in the classification engine is deterministic. However, the Mindbase semantic search used in `get_solution()` may return different matches on different runs if the index has been updated between sessions.\n","numLines":84,"startLine":1,"totalLines":84}}}

What Is Rigorous About This Component\n\nPABLOV enforces a strict artifact-chain model where every stage of execution must produce a verifiable, machine-readable artifact before the pipeline proceeds. This eliminates \"vibes-based\" completion claims entirely.\n\n**Core rigor mechanisms:**\n\n- **Artifact chain completeness**: Five mandatory artifacts form an unbroken chain — `taskspec` (defines work), `expected_set` (defines batch), `worker_handoff` (claims completion), `qa_report` (validates claims), `programmatic_handoff` (proves work via filesystem evidence). Recovery is automatic. `ib_agent_core.md:103`\n- **Five-Step Execution Pattern**: Every agent must follow READ → IDENTIFY → EXECUTE → UPDATE → REPEAT for each checklist item. Violations require task re-execution. `ib_agent_core.md:134-170`\n\n**Rigor verdict**: PABLOV's core insight — that LLM output can only be trusted when it is backed by programmatic, filesystem-verifiable artifacts — is sound and battle-tested. The distinction between \"claim\" (worker_handoff) and \"proof\" (programmatic_handoff) is particularly rigorous.\n\n---\n\n## 2. What Is Bloated / Slow / Expensive\n\n**Complexity overhead:**\n- The five-artifact chain adds significant coordination overhead. Each batch requires creation, tracking, and validation of five separate artifact types.\n- The mandatory sequential pattern (READ → IDENTIFY → EXECUTE → UPDATE → REPEAT, one item at a time) explicitly prohibits parallelism, even when items are independent. `ib_agent_core.md:141-170`\n- The \"mandatory template usage protocol\" adds a full pre-write checklist before every file creation. `ib_agent_core.md:400-413`\n\n**Operational drag:**\n- The bounded correction loop (max 5 per batch) means a single bad batch can cause 5 Worker re-executions + 5 QA re-executions before the system stops. `ib_agent_core.md:559-564`\n- Session management overhead: proactive rollover at 375 messages or 175k tokens means long tasks routinely incur rollover cost even when no quality issue exists. `ib_agent_core.md:920-928`\n\n**Token/runtime expense:**\n- Two full Claude sessions (Worker + QA) per batch. For a 50-item task with batch size 5: 10 Worker sessions + 10 QA sessions + potential correction sessions.\n- `PABLOV_STRICT=false` by default — meaning if the programmatic handoff fails, the batch continues anyway. The rigor is therefore partially opt-in. `ib_agent_core.md:926`\n- Synthesizing a `programmatic_handoff` from conversation mining is expensive (grep over JSONL, jq transforms). This is the fallback path, not the exception.\n\n**Maintenance burden:**\n- Every new task type requires a template. The \"CATASTROPHIC FAILURE WARNING\" for missing templates indicates template compliance is fragile and high-friction. `ib_agent_core.md:401-413`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Execution Model\n\nThe PABLOV execution model is **sequential batch processing with dual-agent loops**:\n\n1. Orchestrator creates `taskspec` with checklist items\n2. Orchestrator generates `expected_set` (batch of N items from unchecked items)\n3. Worker agent executes items one-at-a-time, marks `[x]`, writes `worker_handoff`\n4. DNSP ensures `worker_handoff` exists (detect → nudge → synthesize)\n5. QA agent validates `worker_handoff` against filesystem, writes `qa_report`\n6. If QA fails: items unmarked, Worker receives `qa_report`, correction loop begins\n7. After QA pass: next batch created, cycle repeats\n\n**Quality enforcement**: Enforced at the artifact level (does the artifact exist? does the content match?) not at the intent level. This is a key design choice — programmatic over qualitative.\n\n**Extension points**:\n- `PABLOV_STRICT` flag: makes programmatic handoff failure fatal\n- `PABLOV_INCLUDE_DIFF`: adds git diffs to evidence\n- `PABLOV_FS_FILTER_BY_EVIDENCE`: filters filesystem changes by conversation evidence\n- `AGENT_PROMPT_OVERRIDE`: substitutes custom agent prompts\n- Task `assigned_to` field: auto-detects agent-specific prompts\n\n---\n\n## 4. Pattern Categorization\n\n**Directly Adoptable:**\n- The artifact-chain principle (claim → proof separation) is directly adoptable. The `worker_handoff` (claim) vs `programmatic_handoff` (filesystem proof) distinction is a pattern SuperClaude can adopt without the full machinery.\n- The five-step READ-before-EXECUTE enforcement is directly adoptable as a behavioral rule.\n- DNSP \"never wedge\" principle: always produce an artifact even if synthesized. Adoptable as a fallback guarantee.\n\n**Conditionally Adoptable:**\n- The dual Worker+QA loop is conditionally adoptable. The verification separation is sound, but the cost (two full sessions per batch) is high. A lighter verification pass (single session with self-check) would capture most of the value.\n- Agent Contracts (explicit output requirements per role) are adoptable in lighter form as structured delegation prompts.\n\n**Reject:**\n- The mandatory template pre-read checklist (catastrophic failure warning for every file write) is too high-friction for general use.\n- Sequential-only execution (explicit prohibition on parallel item execution) should be rejected; SuperClaude's parallel-first doctrine is more appropriate for independent items.\n- The full five-artifact chain is too heavy for single-session or lightweight tasks.\n","numLines":86,"startLine":1,"totalLines":86}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_012BeAparp5QpFd7yHwCLwbS","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→component: adversarial-pipeline\n     3→framework: IronClaude\n     4→phase: 3\n     5→generated: 2026-03-14\n     6→evidence_source: auggie-mcp\n     7→---\n     8→\n     9→# Strategy: IronClaude Adversarial Pipeline\n    10→\n    11→## 1. Design Philosophy\n    12→\n    13→The adversarial pipeline exists to produce higher-quality artifacts than any single model can generate by systematically exploiting model diversity: generating multiple variants with different model/persona configurations, then comparing them through structured debate, hybrid scoring, and evidence-tracked merging. The core design principle is **structured disagreement as a quality signal** — divergence between variants reveals assumptions and trade-offs that converged single-model output suppresses.\n    14→\n    15→**Why this design exists**: A single LLM generation tends to commit early to a perspective and rationalize subsequent choices in its favor. By generating two or more variants under different personas (e.g., `opus:architect` vs. `haiku:analyzer`) and running a formal 5-step adversarial protocol, the system forces each variant's assumptions to be made explicit and scored against objective criteria.\n    16→\n    17→**Trade-off**: The 5-step sequential protocol produces 6 artifacts and requires substantial wall-clock time (multiple LLM invocations per step). For simple artifacts where model variance is low (e.g., a trivial config file), the adversarial overhead produces diminishing returns. The protocol is most valuable when comparing architecturally substantive documents where real trade-offs exist.\n    18→\n    19→## 2. Execution Model\n    20→\n    21→The adversarial pipeline operates as a behavioral skill (`.claude/skills/sc-adversarial-protocol/SKILL.md`) with three invocation modes:\n    22→\n    23→**Mode A** — Compare existing files: `--compare file1,file2[,...,fileN]` (2–10 files)\n    24→**Mode B** — Generate variants then compare: `--source <file> --generate <type> --agents <spec>[,...]`\n    25→**Pipeline Mode** — Multi-phase DAG: `--pipeline \"shorthand\"` or `--pipeline @pipeline.yaml`\n    26→\n    27→**5-step sequential protocol** (each step produces a named artifact):\n    28→1. **Diff Analysis** → `diff-analysis.md`: Structural comparison (section ordering, hierarchy), content comparison (claim-level), and contradiction detection across all variants.\n    29→2. **Adversarial Debate** → `debate-transcript.md`: Per-point debate rounds where domain agents argue for their variant's approach. Convergence tracked as `agreed_points / total_diff_points`; threshold configurable (default 0.80). Round 2.5 (invariant probe) activates at `--depth standard|deep`. Max rounds: 1 (quick), 2 (standard), 3 (deep).\n    30→3. **Base Selection** → `base-selection.md`: Hybrid scoring: 50% quantitative (5 metrics: RC×0.30 + IC×0.25 + SR×0.15 + DC×0.15 + SC×0.15) + 50% qualitative (25-criterion additive binary rubric with CEV protocol). Position-bias mitigation via forward + reverse evaluation passes.\n    31→4. **Refactoring Plan** → `refactor-plan.md`: Actionable plan to incorporate non-base variant strengths into the selected base.\n    32→5. **Merge Execution** → `merge-log.md` + merged output: `merge-executor` agent applies refactoring plan changes, adds provenance annotations, validates merged output for structural integrity and cross-reference resolution.\n    33→\n    34→**Tiebreaker protocol** (3 levels, deterministic):\n    35→1. Debate performance (more diff-point wins)\n    36→2. Correctness count (highest correctness criteria count; hallucination-resistant dimension)\n    37→3. Input order (first variant presented wins; arbitrary but deterministic) (`src/superclaude/skills/sc-adversarial-protocol/refs/scoring-protocol.md:189`).\n    38→\n    39→## 3. Quality Enforcement\n    40→\n    41→**CEV (Claim-Evidence-Verdict) protocol**: Every qualitative criterion score must be backed by an explicit evidence citation from the variant text. Unsupported criterion scores are disallowed, preventing hallucinated quality claims.\n    42→\n    43→**Position-bias mitigation**: Qualitative evaluation runs twice per variant — forward and reverse input order — and scores are averaged. This eliminates the systematic LLM preference for items presented earlier in context.\n    44→\n    45→**Convergence plateau detection**: Pipeline Mode includes convergence plateau detection to prevent infinite debate loops when variants have reached maximum achievable agreement below the threshold. The system recognizes plateau and halts rather than continuing fruitless rounds.\n    46→\n    47→**Structural integrity validation**: The `merge-executor` agent performs post-merge validation: heading hierarchy check, section ordering validation, internal reference resolution, and contradiction re-scan on merged content. Any structural break is reported in `merge-log.md`.\n    48→\n    49→**Trade-off**: The 25-criterion qualitative rubric and CEV protocol add significant evaluation time. For quick comparisons where depth of analysis is not required, `--depth quick` reduces to 1 debate round and may skip certain qualitative dimensions, trading thoroughness for speed.\n    50→\n    51→## 4. Error Handling Strategy\n    52→\n    53→**Pipeline resume**: Pipeline Mode writes a manifest tracking phase completion status. Interrupted pipelines can be resumed from the last completed phase without re-executing earlier phases.\n    54→\n    55→**Partial convergence handling**: If debate does not converge to the threshold by the final round, the system records the unconverged state in `debate-transcript.md` and proceeds to scoring with a note indicating unresolved conflicts. The `unresolved_conflicts` count is included in the return contract.\n    56→\n    57→**Merge failure escalation**: If `merge-executor` cannot apply a planned change (e.g., the merge target section does not exist in the base), it reports the issue back to the orchestrator rather than improvising. The `merge-log.md` records which changes failed and why.\n    58→\n    59→**Return contract**: The pipeline returns a structured contract: `merged_output_path`, `convergence_score`, `artifacts_dir`, `status` (success|partial|failed), `base_variant`, `unresolved_conflicts`, `fallback_mode` (`src/superclaude/skills/sc-adversarial-protocol/SKILL.md:412`). Callers can inspect `status` and `unresolved_conflicts` to decide whether to accept the output.\n    60→\n    61→**Trade-off**: The `fallback_mode: true` flag in the return contract signals that some pipeline steps used degraded behavior (e.g., skipped a debate round due to convergence plateau). The caller receives a valid artifact but without the guarantee of full adversarial scrutiny. The fallback condition is transparent but may not be caught by downstream consumers that do not inspect the contract.\n    62→\n    63→## 5. Extension Points\n    64→\n    65→- `--agents model[:persona[:\"instruction\"]]` — per-agent instructions enable fine-grained persona control (e.g., `opus:architect:\"prioritize backward compatibility\"`).\n    66→- `--depth quick|standard|deep` — controls debate rounds (1/2/up to 3) and feature gates (Round 2.5 invariant probe, extended convergence tracking).\n    67→- `--blind` — strips model identity from comparisons, preventing persona-biased evaluations.\n    68→- `--focus` — restricts comparison to specific dimensions, reducing evaluation time for targeted reviews.\n    69→- Pipeline Mode YAML: full DAG specification enables complex multi-phase pipelines with parallel generate phases routed to a single compare phase.\n    70→- `--convergence` threshold configurable (0.50–0.99) — allows looser or tighter convergence requirements per use case.\n    71→\n    72→## 6. System Qualities\n    73→\n    74→**Maintainability**: 5 sequential steps each producing a named artifact means intermediate results are reviewable. Each step has a clear input and output contract. The `merge-executor` agent is strictly plan-following (no strategic decisions), making its behavior predictable.\n    75→\n    76→**Weakness**: The adversarial protocol is implemented entirely in a behavioral skill (SKILL.md), not in compiled code. This makes it impossible to unit-test individual steps without running full Claude sessions. Behavioral regressions in the protocol are difficult to detect without integration tests.\n    77→\n    78→**Checkpoint Reliability**: Pipeline Mode manifest-based resume prevents re-running completed phases on interruption. Single-mode (Mode A/B) has no resume — an interrupted comparison must restart from Step 1.\n    79→\n    80→**Extensibility**: Generic tool design — `/sc:adversarial` is invocable by any SuperClaude command (the roadmap pipeline calls it internally for the debate step). Mode B injectable agents and Pipeline Mode YAML support a wide range of use cases beyond roadmap generation.\n    81→\n    82→**Weakness**: The pipeline produces 6 artifacts in a configurable output directory. There is no cleanup mechanism for orphaned artifact directories from incomplete runs. Long-running projects can accumulate many stale artifact directories.\n    83→\n    84→**Operational Determinism**: Tiebreaker protocol produces deterministic base selection for a given set of debate results. Scoring formula (quant + qual weights) is fixed. Position-bias double-pass produces consistent averaged scores.\n    85→\n    86→**Weakness**: The core generate and debate steps invoke LLM agents whose outputs are non-deterministic. Two identical runs may produce different debate transcripts, different scores, and potentially different base selections — even when the tiebreaker protocol is deterministic, because the debate inputs driving the tiebreaker differ.\n    87→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
